23/10/2020, 22:55 - Lillian Ayoo: Dear Entrepreneur,Our system of education has made us detest failure. In class, we are ranked based on our academic performance, and we look upon those at the bottom, as people who are unlikely to succeed in life.At college, the ranking is gone but replaced with a GPA and a transcript. We get an F and we have to resit. Then we get an A in it, but the previous F still affects our CGPA and is recorded on our transcript.But that’s not how real life works. In the outside world, you fail at something, you learn, you try again more informed, and you succeed. The previous failure is not remembered by anyone, and it doesn’t in any way affects the final success.As a culture, we have learned to reject failure but often we need to relish failure because each circumstance is just another lesson on what to do the next time around to ensure success.As Drew Houston will say, “Don’t worry about failure; you only have to be right once.” And sometimes, we get there by accident, and often it was our previous failures that got us to this point in our lives. Sometimes, failure is a door to a breadth of exciting new opportunities. Don’t let it shut. Open it, and fail.You’re in the real world now and no longer in college; your failure is not recorded, and it will not stop you from achieving excellence.With love,Chidi

03/12/2020, 14:24 - mwavukennedy: Nimekaa hivi nikakumbuka my life as a kid. I'd wonder why during the evening the sun would set in the west but nikiamka naiona ikitokea east. I first asked my grandma and she said she didn't know. She said they were the doings of God. When grandpa came home (Used to work in Nairobi) I posed the question. After a couple of minutes of scratching his bald head he finally said; "Grandson, these white people you keep hearing about (wazungu) do some really amazing things. That same question has bothered me since i was a kid like you, until last week. Me and my coworkers saw on tv what really happens. In the evening as the sun is going down, just before it falls on the ground, the white people place a pickup on it's trajectory and it falls there. Then the driver goes at a very high speed and takes it back to the east, so that when you wake up you see it there." 
As a kid that was the most fascinating thing I'd ever heard. And i believed the old folk, for years. The solar system was one of the most difficult topics to wrap my head around. "But grandpa said...", "But grandpa is always right".

14/01/2021, 08:29 - Nelvine: Austrian economists focus a lot on information and incentives. A major contribution of Hayek was the idea that prices contain and convey information about the real economy. Since then, mainstream economists have produced a variety of fascinating insights rooted in the idea that prices do not only ration scarce goods but also contain valuable information. Another extremely important part of economics is the role of incentives. In my mind, you can boil economics down to the study of incentives and the choices people make given those incentives. Austrian economists like to focus on how incentives influence the decisions people make, recognizing that in order for the economy to function well, you need to avoid making perverse incentives, a problem that government regulations often creates. On the other hand, I would hardly consider these pros of Austrian economics to be solely Austrian; information and incentives are at the heart of mainstream

28/01/2021, 16:12 - Joy Kanyi: 1(a) Total Expenditure for Calculating National Income
It measures GDP as the total sum of expenditure on final goods and services produced in an economy. Using the expenditure approach, national income can be represented as follows: National Income = C (household consumption) + G (government expenditure) + I (investment expense) + NX (net exports).

Factor Incomes for Calculating National Income
It is a process of calculating national income by considering the factors income of an economy. Here, the factor income of every section of and the economy is summed up and then by adding the Net Factor Income from Abroad, National Income is determined.

National Output for Calculating National Income
National income is measured by the output method by calculating the total value of goods and services produced in the country during the year. The money value of goods and services produced in an economy in an accounting year is called Gross National Product (GNP).

(b) I think using the total expenditure to calculate national income is the most appropriate method. This is because when using the national income, some people may not be accounted for in the count. Furthermore, when using national output to calculate national income in the economy, it may include assumptions on subsistence output which may not be accurate

2. Unemployment can be eradicated by:
(i)Reversing rural-urban migration by making rural areas more attractive and capable of providing jobs. This can be done by empowering young people in rural areas to take up more skills and use the resources they have to earn a living. Also introducing geographical subsidies to encourage firms to invest in depressed areas.
(ii)Instituting proper demand management policies that increase aggregate demand including exploiting foreign and regional export markets.  This can be done by increasing government expenditure, cutting taxation or expanding the money supply
(iii)Providing subsidies to firms which reduce working hours rather than the size of the workforce. Lowering taxes on businesses that employ more workers might be effective, for example cuts in employer national insurance contributions for young, low-paid workers
(iv)Reducing welfare payments to the unemployed. To some economists, a policy that reduces the real value of welfare benefits might increase the incentive for the unemployed to take a job. Targeted measures to improve people's incentives might include lowering marginal tax rates for people on low incomes.
(v)Reducing occupational immobility. Immobility is a cause structural unemployment. The government should provide assistance with family relocation to reduce structural unemployment.  This is done by giving recreational facilities, schools, and the quality of life in general in other parts of the country even the provision of financial help to cover moving costs and assist with home purchase.

01/02/2021, 09:26 - Rachael Kanini: plain how hyperinflation might lead to a severe decline in total output.
	With inflation running into the double, triple, quadruple, or even greater number of digits per year, it makes little sense to save.  The only sensible thing to do with money is to spend it before its value is cut in half within a month, a week, or a day.  This very fact of everyone trying to spend as fast as possible will speed the inflationary spiral and cause people to spend more and more time trying to figure out what goods are most likely to go up fastest in price.  More and more people will turn away from productive activity, because wages and salaries are not keeping up with inflation.  Instead, they will spend their time speculating, transferring goods already in existence and producing nothing.
	Eventually, money may become worthless.  No one will work for money.  Barter and living by ones wits become the only means of survival.  Production falls for this reason and also because investment in productive capital practically ceases.  Unemployment soars.  A massive depression is at hand.
01/02/2021, 09:30 - Joy Kanyi: (c)Leakage is withdrawal of spending from the income-expenditures stream. Injection means introduction of income into the flow. Saving is called a leak, because money is not used in the economy in any particular way. So the money has actually leaked out of the economy. A planned investment is usually called an injection. This is simply because capital investments are pumped into the existing economy

01/02/2021, 09:50 - Nelvine: i.	Problems of Definition: Ideally we should include all goods and services produced in the course of the year, but there are some services which are not calculated in terms of money, e.g., services of housewives.
ii.	Inadequate statistical: This makes the task of estimation of national income more acute and difficult.
iii.	Double Counting: Double counting is also an important problem while calculating national income. If the value of all goods and services totaled, the total will overtake the national output, because some goods are currently consumed being used in the making of others. The best way to avoid this error is to calculate only the value of those goods and services that enter into final consumption.
iv.	Choice of Method: The selection of method while calculating National Income is also an important task. The wrong method leads to poor results.
v.	Some information may be unreliable: The reason of illiteracy, most producers has no idea of the quantity and value of their output and do not follow the practice of keeping regular accounts.

01/02/2021, 09:58 - Lillian Ayoo: The ‘underground’ economy. The underground economy consists of illegal and hence undeclared transactions. These could be transactions where the goods or services are themselves illegal, as with drugs, guns and prostitution. Alternatively, they could be transactions that are illegal only in that they are not declared for tax purposes. For example, to avoid paying VAT, a garage may be prepared to repair your car slightly more cheaply if you pay cash. Unemployed people may do casual jobs that they do not declare, to avoid losing benefits.

 Non-marketed goods and services. (e.g. do it yourself decoration and childcare) do not enter GDP calculations and thus understates the level of production in the economy. If there is an increase in employment of specialists such as nannies the rise in GDP will overstate the increase in output

Dangers of double counting. This arises because of the inter-relationship between industries and sectors hence the output of one sector might be the input of the other.

Inadequate information. The sources from which information is obtained are not designed specifically to enable national income to be calculated. There are also some incomes that have to be estimated. Also, some income is not recorded and some information on foreign payments or receipts may not all be recorded.

e)

f) Absolute advantage. A country has absolute advantage over another in the production of a good
if it can produce it with less resources than the other country. For example if Kenya can produce maize with less resources than Tanzania, and Tanzania can produce wheat with less resources than Kenya, then Kenya has an absolute advantage in maize and Tanzania an absolute advantage in wheat. Production of both maize and wheat will be maximized by each country specializing and then trading with the other country. Both will gain.

 Comparative advantage A country has a comparative advantage over another in the production of a good if it can produce it at a lower opportunity cost: i.e. if it has to forgo less of other goods in order to produce it. If countries are to gain from trade, they should export those goods in which they have a comparative advantage and import those goods in which they have a comparative disadvantage
01/02/2021, 10:09 - Joy Kanyi: Answer yangu ya part e ni ndefu sana
01/02/2021, 10:10 - Joy Kanyi: (e)Sterilization is action taken by a country's central bank to counter the effects on the money supply caused by a balance of payments surplus or deficit. Sterilization is most often used in the context of a central bank that takes actions to negate potentially harmful impacts of capital inflows – such as currency appreciation and inflation – both of which can reduce export competitiveness.  A sterilized intervention to prevent currency depreciation is prevented when the country's central bank may decide to intervene in the foreign exchange market. To prop up the value of the nation's currency, the central bank may resort to creating artificial demand for its currency. It can do this by using some of its foreign exchange reserves to buy local currency. The resulting demand stops the currency's depreciation but also acts to reduce the domestic money supply in two ways. First the bank is directly removing some of the nation's currency from circulation as it buys it up. Secondly, if the central bank overshoots the target, the intervention can create or worsen a current account deficit due to the propped-up exchange rate being more favorable for importers than for exporters. This deficit sends currency out of the country, further decreasing liquidity. A sterilized intervention to prevent currency appreciation is when the central bank intervenes on the foreign exchange markets to prevent currency appreciation by selling its own currency for foreign currency-denominated assets, thereby building up its foreign reserves as a happy side effect. However, because the central bank is creating or at least releasing more of its currency into circulation, this will expand the money supply – money spent buying foreign assets initially goes to other countries, but then soon finds its way back into the domestic economy as payment for exports. The expansion of the money supply can cause inflation, which can erode a nation's export competitiveness just as much as currency appreciation would. The classic way to sterilize the inflationary effect of the extra money flowing into the domestic base is for the central bank to use open market operations where it sells bonds domestically, thereby soaking up new cash that would otherwise circulate around the home economy.

01/02/2021, 10:24 - Nelvine: Q1 e)
Sterilization is action taken by a country's central bank to counter the effects on the money supply caused by a balance of payments surplus or deficit. Sterilization is most often used in the context of a central bank that takes actions to negate potentially harmful impacts of capital inflows – such as currency appreciation and inflation – both of which can reduce export competitiveness.
By selling bonds in the domestic market, the central bank prevents the domestic interest rates to converge to the international one, hence inducing more capital inflows and exacerbating the initial problem.
The low maturity of bonds typically used to sterilize increase the vulnerability of the economy.
Higher domestic interest rates bring increased fiscal deficit
The sterilization of capital inflows increases domestic debt and central bank’s deficit in the period of low international interest rates. When the international interest rates rises, the sterilization of capital inflows reduces to relative return of domestic bonds and increases the incentives for a speculative attack in the market which leads the economy to a balance-of-payments constrained ( BOPC)
01/02/2021, 10:25 - Joy Kanyi: (b)There are several types of unemployment present in Kenya today. These include:
(i)Frictional unemployment
This occurs when people are changing jobs. In some cases, it happens when the economy is experiencing full employment. Frictional unemployment can be voluntary since workers make independent decisions and not the employer. In this case, an individual decides to leave their current state of employment to look for work elsewhere. It can also be involuntary where an employer terminates an employee’s contract.
(ii)Structural unemployment
In Kenya, structural unemployment occurs when jobs are available and more people are willing to do them. However, the number of qualified workers available to fill those positions is insufficient. In simple terms, employers are unable to find enough people to work on the jobs and workers are unable to find jobs that need their qualifications. This form of unemployment occurs when there are changes in demand for certain types of labor as economic conditions change.
(iii)Classical unemployment
When the wages employees are willing to accept are more than what the employer is willing to pay, it creates classical unemployment or induced unemployment. In Kenya, classical unemployment happens in two situations; the government sets high minimum wage employers are unwilling to pay or unions such as KNUT and KUPPET negotiate higher benefits and salaries for teachers. Since an employer must pay a higher minimum wage per worker, it means they will only afford to employ fewer workers. A situation will emerge where the employer will have to lay off some employees. The laid off become victims of induced or classical unemployment.
(iv)Casual unemployment
Casual unemployment is widespread in Kenya. It happens when workers employed on contractual terms leave the jobs after the termination of their contracts. As a consequence, it will leave workers unemployed. The workers will have to look for alternative employment options. Casual unemployment is common in industries that hire individuals on a contract basis. These industries include agriculture, film, building and construction.
(v)Cyclical unemployment
In the Kenyan economy, cyclical unemployment occurs when the demand for services or goods cannot affirm full employment. It happens during times of slow economic growth or contraction. It is also directly related to macroeconomic activities in the country. That is the combined or aggregate activity of all entities or persons involved in the economy.

01/02/2021, 11:16 - Joy Kanyi: (a)The five main macroeconomic goals are; non-inflationary growth, low Inflation, low unemployment or full employment, equilibrium in Balance of Payments and fair distribution of income. 
(i)Non-Inflationary Growth
In other words, this is stable and sustainable economic growth and development that is “real” (non-inflationary) over the long-term. Economic growth in an economy is an outward shift in its Production Possibility Curve (PPC). Another way to define growth is the increase in a country’s total output or Gross Domestic Product (GDP). The objective of the central bank and government would be an increase in economic growth without a rise in the rate of inflation. The best way to have economic growth and low inflation is to adopt new technology – which increases productivity. This means higher output for lower cost and lower prices. For example, improved technology in new industries and agriculture could help the productivity of developing economies to catch up with developed economies.

2. Low Inflation
Inflation is the sustained increase in the price level. The rate of inflation is the change in inflation over a period. Central banks would like to keep the growth of the rate at which prices increase at low rates. As inflation rises, every shilling you own buys a smaller percentage of a good or service. Introduction of monetary policy can lower inflation in an economy. If inflation is rising above target, the Central Bank can raise interest rates. Higher interest rates raise the cost of borrowing, reduce lending and consumer spending. This moderates economic growth and reduces inflationary pressure.

3. Low Unemployment or Full Employment
Full employment occurs when the labor force (this counts as people who are actively seeking jobs or are already employed) is fully employed in productive work. A person is considered to be unemployed if he doesn’t currently doesn’t have a job and is actively searching for one. Having a lower rate of unemployment means that the economy is more productive. This objective means that as many people who want to be employed are employed, so the economy is running at or near full productivity. To obtain full employment for all, targeted employment policies need to be undertaken that can direct jobs to areas of high unemployment. The tool for this is the public and non-profit employment programs that create jobs by meeting unmet needs. 

4. Equilibrium in Balance of Payments
Equilibrium in Balance of Payments means that a country’s exports or imports should not be much larger than its imports or exports. Having a large balance of payments deficit or surplus is not beneficial for the economy. Equilibrium in a country's economy can be achieved by improving the balance of trade through import restrictions and measures of export promotion. Since balance of payments becomes adverse chiefly on account of excess of imports over exports, the most urgent steps are to be taken in this direction. A country having an adverse balance of payments must to check imports, or to stimulate exports, or do both. Imports can be checked either by total prohibition, or by levying import duties

5. Fair Distribution of Income
A fair or equitable distribution of income means that the gap between the rich and the poor is not too large. Fair or equitable doesn’t mean equal, but fair is a relative concept. What could be fair to one person, may not be fair to another. The government doesn’t want all the wealth concentrated with a small group of people.

01/02/2021, 11:17 - Nelvine: Q3 c)
(i)	Open Market Operations
Through open market operations, the Bank buys or sells securities in the secondary market in order to achieve a desired level of Bank reserves. To increase money supply in the economy, the Bank injects money into the economy through buying securities in exchange for money stock. As the law of supply and demand takes effect to determine the cost of credit (interest rates) in the money market, money stock adjusts itself to the desired level
(ii)	Discount window operations
The Bank, as lender of last resort, may provide secured short-term loans to commercial banks on overnight basis at punitive rates, this injects money in the economy hence increasing money supply thus restricting banks to seek funding in the market resorting to Central Bank funds only as a last solution. The discount rate is set by the Central Bank to reflect the monetary policy objectives.
(iii)	Reserve Requirements
The Central Bank is empowered by the law to retain a certain proportion of commercial banks' deposits to be held as non-interest bearing reserves at the Central Bank. An decrease in reserve requirements allows commercial banks’ ability to expand bank credit and this results in credit easing. This in turn injects more money in the economy hence increasing its supply.
(iv)	Central Bank Rate (CBR)
The CBR is reviewed and announced by the Monetary Policy Committee (MPC) at least every two months. Movements in the CBR, both in direction and magnitude, signal the monetary policy stance. In order to enhance clarity and certainty in monetary policy implementation, the CBR is the base for all monetary policy operations.
Whenever the Central Bank is injecting liquidity through a Reverse Repo, the CBR is the lowest acceptable rate by law. This allows for more supply of money in the economy
(v)	Foreign Exchange Market Operations
The CBK can also inject or withdraw liquidity from the banking system by engaging in foreign exchange transactions. A purchase of foreign exchange injects liquidity into the system hence increasing money supply in the economy

01/02/2021, 11:30 - Joy Kanyi: 5. Fair Distribution of Income
A fair or equitable distribution of income means that the gap between the rich and the poor is not too large. Fair or equitable doesn’t mean equal, but fair is a relative concept. What could be fair to one person, may not be fair to another. The government doesn’t want all the wealth concentrated with a small group of people. Governments can influence income distribution by their policies towards asset distribution, by the growth strategy chosen and by tax and expenditure policies. Well designed, tax,
expenditure and transfer policies can greatly improve the distribution of welfare. The types of policies likely to improve income distribution include agrarian-focused and employment-intensive growth strategies, high and widely spread expenditure on education, redistribution of assets, a structured market to direct education, training, and asset accumulation towards deprived groups and strong policies towards social protection and social income.

21/04/2021, 14:48 - Joy Kanyi: *CAREER TALK: Demystifying Agricultural Insurance*

_Syngenta foundation for sustainable agriculture (SFSA)_

Key messages 
> Food security and poverty reduction depend on services provided by well functioning agricultural value chain systems.
> Climate shock is making the agricultural value chains and global food system highly vulnerable to shocks.

Risks faced
>Weather related risks; crops are sensitive to weather parameters eg rainfall and temperature. 
> Market prices and policy related risks; government and company policies are placed to regulate the market, market prices shift based on the supply and demand of agricultural produce
> Production related risks; differs from one farmer to another based on skills and cultural setup, farmer agricultural practices include how ploughing is done; land, soil and biodiversity also affects production and so does pests, diseases and weeds
> Political risks; political instability affects small scale farmers
> Health risks; a farmer might fall sick and this may affect the general production

Emerging markets
1. Technology
2. Climate risk
3. Food security
4. Pandemics

>Diversify your knowledge and interests into these new markets. Don't stay boxed in the traditional insurance sector
>Look at global issues and come up with models that could be relevant in solving them
> Data is the first step in finding an effective solution so delve deep into it
> Technology is very important so explore it as much as you can
> Find innovative ways in which you can raise funds to pay for your professional papers. Proper budget planning and delayed gratification comes in handy.

What if Africa is just a sleeping lion?

Something about Africa is beginning to intrigue me. 
There's something about the knowledge I've been consuming lately that's making me wake up at 4am, just before my alarm goes off.
